(قَوْلُهُ: أَيْ: وَإِنْ لَمْ فسَّرَ لَا» بـ «لَمْ» ؛ إشارة إلى أنَّ هذهِ الأحكام استقرَّتْ ها ومضَتْ ؛ و «لا» التي لنفي المستقبل ؛ ليسَتْ على ظاهرِهـ (قَوْلُهُ : فَأَدَاةٌ) سُمّي بذلك ؛ لأَنَّهُ يؤدَّى به معنى كلمةٍ لِأُخرى، وقضيَّتُهُ : أَنَّ الضّمير أداة ، وذلك لأنَّهُ لَا يستقل بالإخبارِ بِهِ؛ لعدم استقلاله بإفادته معناه، بل يفتقرُ في إفادتِهِ لشيءٍ آخَرَ كالتَّكلم والخطاب والمرجع ، أنَّه ليس بأداة نعم ما يقوم مقامه - وهو الظَّاهرُ - مستقل بالإخبار بهِ، فَالمراد مستقل بنفْسِهِ أو مَا يقوم مقامه
(قَوْلُهُ: وَعِنْدَ النُّحَاةِ : حَرْفٌ) ظاهرُ كلام المصنِّف : أنَّ الأداةَ عند المناطقةِ مرادفة للحرفِ عندَ النُّحاة، وليس كذلك ؛ لأنَّ الأداة شاملة للحروفِ وبعض الأسماءِ كَأسماء الشروط، وقد يُجاب عن الشارح : بأنَّهُ نظرَ لِلغالب، تأمَّل.
(قَوْلُهُ: وَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَقِلَّ ... إلخ) فيهِ مَا تقدَّمَ قالَ السَّيِّدُ: يشكل هذا بمثل الضَّمائرِ المتّصلةِ كَالأَلفِ في ضَرَبَا، والواو في ضَربُوا ، والكافِ في ضَرَبَكَ، والياء في غُلامِي؛ فإِنَّ شَيئاً مِن هذهِ الضَّمائر لا يصلح لأن يخبرَ بِهِ وحدَهُ، وربَّما يُجَابُ بأنَّ المراد من عدم صلاحيَّةِ الأداةِ لِأَنْ يُخبرَ بِهَا وحدَهَا، أَنَّهَا لا تصلحُ لِذَلِكَ لا بِنَفْسِهَا وَلَا بِمَا يُرادِفُها، وتِلْكَ الضَّمائر تصلحُ لِأَنْ يُخبرَ بِمَا يُرادفُها ، فإِنَّ الأَلِفَ في ضَرَبَا بمعنى: هُمَا، والواو في ضَرَبُوا بمعنى : هُمْ ، والكافُ في ضَرَبَكَ بمعنى أنتَ ، والياء في غُلامِي بمعنى أنا ، وهذهِ المرادفات تصلح لأَن يخبر بها وحدها، فإِنْ قُلْتَ: الأسماء الموصولة لا تصلح لأنْ يخبر بها وحدها؛ فيجب أن تكونَ أداةً ، والجواب : أنَّها صالحة لذلك، لكنَّها لإبهامها تحتاج إلى صِلَةٍ تُبيِّنُهَا ، فالمحكوم به أو المحكوم عليهِ هُوَ الموصول ، والصَّلَةُ خارجة عنهُ مُبَيِّنَةٌ لَهُ.
(قَوْلُهُ : فَأَدَاةٌ) قالَ الجَلالُ : تدخل فيها الكلماتُ الوجوديَّةُ كَـ : «كَانَ» النَّاقصة وأخواتها، ونِسبتُها إلى الأفعالِ كَنِسبةِ الأدواتِ إلى الأسماء، فإنْ كانَ مثلاً لا يدلُّ على الكَوْنِ فِي نَفْسِهِ بَلْ عَلى كَوْنِ شَيْءٍ شيئاً ، لم يُذكَرْ؛ فَهَذِهِ الكلماتُ إنَّما تدلُّ على نسبة شيء إلى موضوع غيرِ مُعيَّنٍ في زمانٍ مُعيَّنٍ ؛ تكونُ تِلكَ النِّسبةُ لِمعنى مُنتظَر .ا.هـ. ومعنى كَوْنِ نِسبتها إلى الأفعالِ ... إلخ؛ أنَّ الأدواتِ تُشارِكُ الأسماء في عدم الدَّلالةِ بالهيئة على الزَّمانِ وتُفَارِقُها فى الاستقلال وعَدَمِهِ، كَذلِكَ الكلمات الوجوديَّةُ؛ تُشارِكُ الأفعال التَّامَّةَ في الدَّلالةِ على الزَّمانِ وتُفَارِقُها في الاستقلال، وعدمه، وإِنَّما سُمِّيَتْ وُجوديَّةٌ؛ لأنَّ الكَوْنَ يُرادِفُ الوجود وهو قسمان؛ أحدهما : وجود شيءٍ في نَفْسِهِ كَوجودِ زيدٍ وَوجودِ البياض في نَفْسِهِ، والآخَرُ: وجودُ الشَّيء لِغَيرِهِ كَوجودِ البياض للجسم؛ ويُسمَّى وُجوداً لغيرِهِ وَوُجوداً رابطيًّا ونسبيًّا، والأَوَّلُ هو مدلول «كانَ» التَّامَّةِ، والثَّاني مدلول «كَانَ» النَّاقصة.
And if not: meaning if it does not independent by informing with it alone, then it is a tool, and according to grammarians: a particle. (His statement: meaning: and if not, he interpreted 'la' with 'lam' indicating that these rulings have been established here and passed; and 'la' which negates the future is not apparent.) (His statement: tool) it was named that because the meaning of a word is conveyed to another; and its implication is that the pronoun is a tool because it is not independent for informing, due to its lack of independence in conveying its meaning, but it depends in its conveyance on something else like the speaker, the addressee, and the referent. It is not a tool; rather, what takes its place - which is the apparent - is independent for informing. So what is meant is independent by itself or what takes its place. (His statement: and according to grammarians: a particle) The apparent meaning of the author's words is that tool among logicians is synonymous with particle among grammarians, but it is not so because tool includes particles and some names like the names of conditions. And it can be answered about the commentator: that he considered the majority, reflect. (His statement: and if it is not independent... etc.) In it is what preceded. al-Sayyid said: This is problematic with attached pronouns like the alif in ḍarabā, the waw in ḍarabū, the kaf in ḍarabaka, the ya in ghulāmī; for none of these pronouns is suitable to be informed with it alone. And it can be answered: that what is meant by the tool's lack of suitability to be informed by it alone is that it is not suitable for that neither by itself nor by what is synonymous with it. And those pronouns are suitable for informing with what is synonymous with them. For the alif in ḍarabā means humā, the waw in ḍarabū means hum, the kaf in ḍarabaka means anta, and the ya in ghulāmī means anā. And these synonyms are suitable for informing with them alone. If you say: the relative pronouns are not suitable for informing with them alone, so they must be tools. The answer: they are suitable for that, but due to their vagueness they need a link to clarify them, so the subject of judgment or predicate is the relative pronoun, and the link is external clarifying it. (His statement: tool) al-Jalāl said: including the existential words like the incomplete 'kāna' and its sisters, and their relation to verbs is like the relation of tools to nouns. For example, 'in' does not denote existence in itself but denotes existence of something as something, it is not mentioned; so these words only denote a relation of something to an unspecified subject in a specified time; that relation is for a meaning to be waited. End. And the meaning of their relation to verbs... etc. is that tools share with nouns in not indicating time by form, and differ in independence and its lack. Similarly, existential words share with complete verbs in indicating time, and differ in independence and its lack. They were called existential because 'existence' is synonymous with being, and it has two types: one: existence of a thing in itself like existence of Zayd and existence of whiteness in itself; the other: existence of a thing for another like existence of whiteness for the body; it is called existence for another, connecting existence, and relational. The first is the meaning of the complete 'kāna', and the second is the meaning of the incomplete 'kāna'.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of 'tool' (adāh) in logic. It begins by restating the rule: if a word cannot independently convey a complete meaning (i.e., serve as a subject or predicate of a proposition), then it is a tool. According to grammarians, such words are called particles (ḥarf). The commentator then clarifies that the author's use of 'lā' here is for past tense, not future. The name 'tool' is given because it conveys the meaning of another word. The passage then addresses a potential objection: pronouns like the attached pronouns (e.g., the alif meaning 'they two') seem to be tools because they cannot stand alone in informing. The answer is that the definition considers not only the word itself but also its synonyms; pronouns have independent synonyms (e.g., 'humā' for the alif), so they are not tools. Similarly, relative pronouns (al-mawṣūlāt) are not tools because although they are vague, they serve as subjects/predicates themselves, and the linking clause (ṣila) is external. The commentator then includes a discussion from al-Jalāl about existential words like the incomplete 'kāna' and its sisters. These words, like tools, are not independent in informing; they indicate a relation (e.g., Zayd was standing). They share with verbs in indicating time but differ in independence. The term 'existential' is explained: existence can be of a thing in itself (e.g., Zayd's existence) or of a thing for another (e.g., whiteness for the body). The complete 'kāna' indicates the first, the incomplete 'kāna' the second.

Key Terms
أداة
حرف
ضمير
كان الناقصة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is an attached pronoun like the alif in 'ḍarabā' not a tool?

B) Because it has an independent synonym (humā) that can be informed with.

D) Because it is a particle in grammar.

Key Takeaway
A logical tool is a word that cannot independently serve as a subject or predicate, considering both the word itself and its synonyms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Distinguishing Logical Tool (Adāh) from Grammatical Particle (Ḥarf)
Commentary clarifies that adāh is not synonymous with ḥarf, as logic includes some nouns.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given word is a logical tool only, a grammatical particle only, both, or neither.

Core Idea
Logic's 'tool' is broader than grammar's 'particle'; it includes condition names and other nouns.

The commentator warns against equating the logical term adāh with the grammatical term ḥarf. While many tools are particles, logic also considers certain nouns as tools. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion when reading logical texts and applying them to Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Recall the grammatical definition
In Arabic grammar, ḥarf is a part of speech that does not inflect and indicates meaning in others. Examples: 'fī', 'hal', 'wa'
2
Recall the logical definition
In logic, adāh is any word that cannot independently be a subject or predicate. This includes all grammatical particles and some nouns.
3
Find the overlap and difference
All ḥurūf are adawāt, but not all adawāt are ḥurūf. The passage gives 'names of conditions' (asmā' al-shurūṭ) as examples of nouns that are tools.
Condition names like 'man' (whoever) or 'mata' (when) are nouns in grammar but function as tools because they cannot be subjects/predicates alone.
4
Test with examples
Consider 'hal' (interrogative particle): it is both a particle and a tool. Consider 'man' (condition noun): it is a noun in grammar but a tool in logic. Consider 'Zaydun': it is a noun and not a tool.
The commentator suggests the author's equation was for the majority, but careful inspection shows the difference.

And if not: meaning if it does not independent by informing with it alone, then it is a tool, and according to grammarians: a particle. (His statement: meaning: and if not, he interpreted 'la' with 'lam' indicating that these rulings have been established here and passed; and 'la' which negates the future is not apparent.) (His statement: tool) it was named that because the meaning of a word is conveyed to another; and its implication is that the pronoun is a tool because it is not independent for informing, due to its lack of independence in conveying its meaning, but it depends in its conveyance on something else like the speaker, the addressee, and the referent. It is not a tool; rather, what takes its place - which is the apparent - is independent for informing. So what is meant is independent by itself or what takes its place. (His statement: and according to grammarians: a particle) The apparent meaning of the author's words is that tool among logicians is synonymous with particle among grammarians, but it is not so because tool includes particles and some names like the names of conditions. And it can be answered about the commentator: that he considered the majority, reflect. (His statement: and if it is not independent... etc.) In it is what preceded. al-Sayyid said: This is problematic with attached pronouns like the alif in ḍarabā, the waw in ḍarabū, the kaf in ḍarabaka, the ya in ghulāmī; for none of these pronouns is suitable to be informed with it alone. And it can be answered: that what is meant by the tool's lack of suitability to be informed by it alone is that it is not suitable for that neither by itself nor by what is synonymous with it. And those pronouns are suitable for informing with what is synonymous with them. For the alif in ḍarabā means humā, the waw in ḍarabū means hum, the kaf in ḍarabaka means anta, and the ya in ghulāmī means anā. And these synonyms are suitable for informing with them alone. If you say: the relative pronouns are not suitable for informing with them alone, so they must be tools. The answer: they are suitable for that, but due to their vagueness they need a link to clarify them, so the subject of judgment or predicate is the relative pronoun, and the link is external clarifying it. (His statement: tool) al-Jalāl said: including the existential words like the incomplete 'kāna' and its sisters, and their relation to verbs is like the relation of tools to nouns. For example, 'in' does not denote existence in itself but denotes existence of something as something, it is not mentioned; so these words only denote a relation of something to an unspecified subject in a specified time; that relation is for a meaning to be waited. End. And the meaning of their relation to verbs... etc. is that tools share with nouns in not indicating time by form, and differ in independence and its lack. Similarly, existential words share with complete verbs in indicating time, and differ in independence and its lack. They were called existential because 'existence' is synonymous with being, and it has two types: one: existence of a thing in itself like existence of Zayd and existence of whiteness in itself; the other: existence of a thing for another like existence of whiteness for the body; it is called existence for another, connecting existence, and relational. The first is the meaning of the complete 'kāna', and the second is the meaning of the incomplete 'kāna'.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of 'tool' (adāh) in logic. It begins by restating the rule: if a word cannot independently convey a complete meaning (i.e., serve as a subject or predicate of a proposition), then it is a tool. According to grammarians, such words are called particles (ḥarf). The commentator then clarifies that the author's use of 'lā' here is for past tense, not future. The name 'tool' is given because it conveys the meaning of another word. The passage then addresses a potential objection: pronouns like the attached pronouns (e.g., the alif meaning 'they two') seem to be tools because they cannot stand alone in informing. The answer is that the definition considers not only the word itself but also its synonyms; pronouns have independent synonyms (e.g., 'humā' for the alif), so they are not tools. Similarly, relative pronouns (al-mawṣūlāt) are not tools because although they are vague, they serve as subjects/predicates themselves, and the linking clause (ṣila) is external. The commentator then includes a discussion from al-Jalāl about existential words like the incomplete 'kāna' and its sisters. These words, like tools, are not independent in informing; they indicate a relation (e.g., Zayd was standing). They share with verbs in indicating time but differ in independence. The term 'existential' is explained: existence can be of a thing in itself (e.g., Zayd's existence) or of a thing for another (e.g., whiteness for the body). The complete 'kāna' indicates the first, the incomplete 'kāna' the second.

Existential Words as Logical Tools
Commentary includes existential words (like incomplete kāna) as tools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why incomplete 'kāna' and similar verbs are considered logical tools and distinguish them from complete verbs.

Core Idea
Existential words like incomplete 'kāna' are tools because they indicate a relation, not an independent state.

The passage concludes with a discussion of existential words (al-kalimāt al-wujūdiyyah), such as the incomplete verb 'kāna'. These words share with tools the lack of independent meaning, but they also indicate time, unlike typical tools. Understanding their nature is crucial for analyzing propositions in logic and theology.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two types of existence
Existence can be of a thing in itself (e.g., Zayd's existence) or of a thing for another (e.g., whiteness existing in a body). The complete 'kāna' indicates the first, the incomplete 'kāna' the second.
2
Identify the function of incomplete 'kāna'
Incomplete 'kāna' (e.g., 'Zayd was standing') indicates a relation (nisbah) between a subject and predicate. This relation is not independent.
It requires both a subject and predicate to complete the meaning.
3
Compare with tools
Tools like 'fī' also indicate a relation (e.g., Zayd fī al-dār). Both do not stand alone. But 'kāna' also indicates time, unlike most tools.
Tools share with nouns in not indicating time, but existential words share with verbs in indicating time.
4
Classify existential words as tools
Because they lack independence, they are included in the logical definition of tool. The commentator al-Jalāl explicitly includes them.
They are called existential because they express a mode of existence (relation).

(قَوْلُهُ: أَيْ: وَإِنْ لَمْ فسَّرَ لَا» بـ «لَمْ» ؛ إشارة إلى أنَّ هذهِ الأحكام استقرَّتْ ها ومضَتْ ؛ و «لا» التي لنفي المستقبل ؛ ليسَتْ على ظاهرِهـ (قَوْلُهُ : فَأَدَاةٌ) سُمّي بذلك ؛ لأَنَّهُ يؤدَّى به معنى كلمةٍ لِأُخرى، وقضيَّتُهُ : أَنَّ الضّمير أداة ، وذلك لأنَّهُ لَا يستقل بالإخبارِ بِهِ؛ لعدم استقلاله بإفادته معناه، بل يفتقرُ في إفادتِهِ لشيءٍ آخَرَ كالتَّكلم والخطاب والمرجع ، أنَّه ليس بأداة نعم ما يقوم مقامه - وهو الظَّاهرُ - مستقل بالإخبار بهِ، فَالمراد مستقل بنفْسِهِ أو مَا يقوم مقامه

The Seven Divisions Apply Only to Nouns
Commentator critiques the author's generalization of the sevenfold classification to all singulars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which of the seven divisions of the singular are restricted to nouns and explain the commentator's refinement of the muqassam.

Core Idea
Tawāṭu', tashkīk, and alam are exclusive to nouns — the sevenfold classification of the singular actually targets nouns only.

In his chapter on expressions, the author of the matn appears to apply the seven divisions to all singular words—nouns, verbs, and particles. However, the commentator objects: three of those divisions (univocity, ambiguity by priority, and proper nouns) are inherently tied to the conceptual properties of nouns alone. This lesson examines the commentator's critique and his proposed restriction of the divided (muqassam) to nouns, following al-Kātibī's approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the restricted divisions
Extract from the passage the three divisions that the commentator says 'only occur in the noun' (tawāṭu', tashkīk, and alam).
These are specific to nouns; verbs and particles are excluded.
2
Understand why they are noun-specific
Reflect on each term: tawāṭu' (univocity) applies to common nouns like 'insān'; tashkīk (ambiguity by priority) applies to terms like 'wujūd'; alam (proper noun) is inherently a noun category.
Verbs and particles lack the semantic properties that support these divisions.
3
Contrast the author and commentator
The author's apparent position is that all singulars (including verbs and particles) are divided into the seven divisions. The commentator says 'it is not so'.
This is the central point of criticism.
4
Examine the proposed solution and defense
The commentator suggests restricting the muqassam to nouns alone, as al-Kātibī did. He then offers a possible rejoinder: the author intended the singular only insofar as it is realized as a noun.
This subtlety reconciles the wording with the proper scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مباحثِ الألفاظ. وأمَّا التَّواطُقُ والتَّشكَّكُ فَلَا يجريان إلا في الاسم، وكذلكَ العَلَمُ. وظاهرُ المصنف أنَّ كلَّ واحدٍ مِن أقسام المفرد؛ سواء كان اسماً أو فعلاً أو أداة؛ ينقسم إلى هذهِ الأقسام السَّبعة، وليس كذلك، فكانَ الأَوْلَى لِلمصنِّفِ جعلُ المقسَّمِ الاسم خاصَّة كَمَا فعل الكاتبيُّ، وإن كان يمكنُ الجواب عن المصنِّف بأنَّ المراد بالمفردِ الَّذي جعلهُ مُقسَّماً لهذه الأقسام السبعة المفرد من حيثُ تحققه الاسم لا المفرد من حيثُ هو، فَتَأمَّل.
Chapter on the investigation of expressions. As for tawāṭu' (univocity) and tashkīk (ambiguity by priority), they only occur in the noun, and likewise the proper noun (alam). The apparent meaning of the author is that every one of the divisions of the singular, whether it is a noun, a verb, or a particle, is divided into these seven divisions, but it is not so. It would have been better for the author to make the divided (muqassam) specifically the noun, as al-Kātibī did, although it is possible to answer on behalf of the author by saying that what is intended by the singular which he made as the divided for these seven divisions is the singular in respect of its realization as a noun, not the singular in respect of itself. So reflect.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (taʿlīqa) on the author's classification of the singular (mufrad) into seven divisions. The commentator begins by asserting that two of the divisions—tawāṭu' (univocity) and tashkīk (ambiguity by priority)—apply exclusively to nouns, not to verbs or particles. Similarly, the category of alam (proper noun) is also limited to nouns. He then points out that the author's apparent position is that every type of singular expression—whether noun, verb, or particle—can be divided into the seven divisions (i.e., mushakkak, mutawāṭi', mutarādif, mushtarak, manqūl, murtajal, and ṣāḥib al-waḍʿ al-ʿaẓmī). However, this is not correct, because tawāṭu', tashkīk, and alam only make sense for nouns. The commentator suggests that it would have been better for the author to restrict the divided (muqassam) to the noun alone, following the method of al-Kātibī (the author of the Shamsiyya). Nevertheless, he offers a possible defense of the author: the singular referred to as the divided is not the singular absolutely, but only insofar as it is realized as a noun. In other words, the classification implicitly targets only nouns, even though the wording appears general. The commentator advises the reader to reflect on this subtle point.

Key Takeaway
The commentator restricts the sevenfold classification of the singular to nouns, because tawāṭu', tashkīk, and alam are inherently noun-specific.

The Two Conditions for Proper Nouns: Tashakhkhus and Wad'an
Commentators explain the definition of 'alam and the need for the wad'an restriction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two conditions in the definition of a proper noun ('alam) and explain why the restriction 'wad'an' is necessary.

Core Idea
A proper noun must have a single individuated meaning by original linguistic convention, not by usage.

The definition of 'alam in the matn states: 'If its meaning is one, then with its individuation (wad'an)'. This lesson unpacks the meaning of tashakhkhus (individuation) and the role of the qualifier 'wad'an'. The commentaries clarify that tashakhkhus here means the meaning is particular to an external individual, and 'wad'an' ensures that the individuation is inherent in the linguistic convention, not accidental from usage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Find the phrases in the matn: 'if its meaning is one' (إن اتحد معناه) and 'then with its individuation (wad'an)' (فمع تشخصه وضعا). These are the two conditions for a proper noun.
2
Understand tashakhkhus
Al-Dasuqi explains that tashakhkhus means the meaning is determined externally (خارجاً), not just mentally. The meaning cannot be predicated of many; it is particular.
Mental individuation exists in all concepts, so that is not sufficient.
3
Analyze the wad'an restriction
The word 'wad'an' (by original convention) specifies that the individuation comes from the original linguistic assignment. This excludes words where particularity arises only from usage, such as pronouns.
Without this restriction, pronouns would be considered proper nouns because they refer to specific individuals in context.
4
See the consequence of omitting wad'an
If wad'an were not included, pronouns, demonstratives, and relative pronouns would fit the definition because they are used for specific individuals. But since they are universal in wad', they are excluded only by the wad'an restriction.
The hashia discusses that if the first condition is taken as the meaning assigned by wad', then wad'an might be redundant, but the commentator clarifies its necessity.

(إِنِ اتَّحَدَ مَعْنَاهُ فَمَعَ تَشَخْصِهِ)؛ أي: تشخص ذلك المعنى (وَضْعَاً)
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ: تَشَخْصِهِ) أي: تعين ذلك المعنى خارجاً لا في الذهن، وإلا فالتشخص الذهني موجودٌ في الجميع
واعلَمْ أَنَّ المرادَ بِتشخُص المعنى؛ أن لا يكون صالحاً لأن يُقال على كثيرين، وبعدمِ تَشخُصِ معناه أن يكون صالحاً لأن يُقال على كثيرين.
(قَوْلُهُ: وَضْعَاً) تمييز؛ أي: من جهة الوضع خرج الضمير، واسم الإشارة، واسم الموصول، فهي كُلِّيَّةٌ وَضْعاً، جُزئيَّةٌ استعمالاً، على مذهب المصنّف، وحينئذ فتشخُصُ معناها عارض بواسطة الاستعمالات، مثلاً: الذي وضعَ لِلمفردِ المذكَّر، وهذا كُلّيّ وتعينه عارض؛ لأنَّهُ إِنَّما جاءَ من الصلة؛ لأنَّنا قبل «ما» تأتي لم نعلم الَّذي من هو. ا.هـ. تقرير.
العطار
المحشّي على إيرادِ الحرفِ فَقَطْ؛ مَعَ جريان ذلك في بقيَّةِ ما هو موضوع بالوضع العام للموضوع لَهُ الخاص، فإنَّ البحثَ إِنَّمَا يَتَّجِهُ على القولِ بِهِ.
(قَوْلُهُ: إِنِ اتَّحَدَ مَعْنَاهُ) بمعنى أَنَّهُ لا يكونُ لَهُ مَعنيان، وبحث في الحاشية بِمَا حاصلُهُ أَنَّهُ إِنْ كانَ المراد المعنى الموضوعَ لَهُ؛ فَلا حاجة إلى قيد: وضعاً، في تعريف العَلَم، ولا يصحُ جَعْلُ اللَّفْظِ بالقياس إلى المعنى الحقيقي والمجازي مِنَ القِسم الثَّاني وإنْ كانَ أعمَّ؛ فَمَعَ استدراكِ قَيْد: وضعاً؛ يخفى وجود لفظ اتَّحَدَ معناهُ؛ لأنَّهُ يخصُّ لَفْظاً لمْ يُوضَعْ إِلا لِمعنى بسيط لا لازِمَ لَهُ، وفي وُجودِهِ خفاءٌ، ويلزم أن يَتَّصِفَ اللَّفْظُ بِالتَّواطئ والتَّشكيكِ بالنَّظر إلى المعنى الغيرِ الموضوع له، وأنَّه خارجي.
(۱) (قَوْلُهُ: خرجَ الضَّمير... إلخ) فيه أن الضّمائر وأسماء الإشارة والموصولات كليات وضعاً عند المصنّف، فكيف يعقل تشخّص معناها خارجاً مع كونه كلّيًّا وقد سبق أن التشخص هنا وأن معناه عدم صحة الحمل على كثيرين، وهذا ينافي كلِّيَّتها وحينئذ فهي خارجة بقول المصنف: فمع تشخصه، واستعمالها في مشخص استعمال لها في غير ما وضعت له عنده، والكلام في تشخص الموضوع له حقيقة، وعليه فيلزم استدراك قوله: وضعاً، وأما عند السيد والعضد من أنها جزئيات وضعاً واستعمالاً فهي خارجة بقوله: إن اتَّحد معناه، لا بقوله: وضعاً كما لا يخفى. ا.هـ.
الشرنوبي.
('If its meaning is one, then with its individuation (wad'an)') i.e., the individuation of that meaning (wad'an). Al-Dasuqi: (His statement: 'its individuation') i.e., the determination of that meaning externally, not in the mind, otherwise mental individuation exists in everything. And know that what is meant by the individuation of the meaning is that it is not fit to be said of many, and by the absence of individuation of its meaning that it is fit to be said of many. (His statement: 'wad'an') is a specification; i.e., in terms of linguistic convention, the pronoun, the demonstrative, and the relative pronoun are excluded, for they are universals in wad' and particulars in usage, according to the author's opinion. Thus the individuation of their meaning is accidental by way of usages. For example: 'alladhi' was placed for the singular masculine, and this is universal, and its particularization is accidental because it only comes from the relative clause, since before the 'ma' comes we do not know who 'alladhi' refers to. End of report. Al-'Attar: The commentator on the objection of the particle alone, with that running in the rest of what is placed with a general wad' for a specific subject, for the inquiry is only directed at that opinion. (His statement: 'if its meaning is one') means that it does not have two meanings. And there is a discussion in the hashia whose summary is: if what is meant is the meaning for which it was placed, then there is no need for the restriction 'wad'an' in the definition of proper noun, and it is not valid to consider the word by way of the real and metaphorical meaning from the second division even if it is more general; because with the addition of the restriction 'wad'an', the existence of the phrase 'if its meaning is one' is obscure, because it specifies a word that was placed only for a simple meaning with no necessary concomitant, and its existence is obscure. And it would necessitate that the word be described by univocity and amphibolous with regard to the meaning not originally placed for it, and that it is external. (Note 1): (His statement: 'the pronoun came out... etc.') In it, pronouns, demonstratives, and relative pronouns are universals in wad' according to the author. So how can the individuation of their meaning externally be understood when they are universal? And it has preceded that tashakhkhus here means the inability to be predicated of many, and this contradicts their universality. Then they are excluded by the author's statement: 'then with its individuation', and their usage for a specific individual is usage in other than what they were placed for according to him. The discussion is about the individuation of the subject for which it was placed in reality. Therefore, the addition of his statement 'wad'an' is necessary. But according to al-Sayyid and al-'Adud, they are particulars in wad' and usage, so they are excluded by his statement: 'if its meaning is one', not by his statement: 'wad'an', as is not hidden. End. Al-Sharnubi.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a definitional commentary on the definition of a proper noun (علم). It begins with a phrase from the matn: 'If its meaning is one, then with its individuation (wad'an)'. The commentator explains that 'individuation' (تشخص) means the meaning is determined as a specific external entity, not just in the mind, because mental individuation applies to all concepts. The intended understanding of tashakhkhus is that the meaning cannot be predicated of many (i.e., it is particular). Then the restriction 'wad'an' (linguistic convention) is clarified: it signifies that the individuation comes from the original linguistic assignment, not from usage. This excludes pronouns, demonstratives, and relative pronouns, which, according to the author, are universal in wad' but become particular in usage. For example, the word 'alladhi' is placed for the singular masculine in general, but its specific reference comes from the relative clause. Al-'Attar notes that the objection about the particle alone is addressed, and the inquiry only arises if one accepts the general wad' for a specific subject. Next, a discussion from the hashia is summarized: if the intended meaning is the actual meaning assigned by wad', then the restriction 'wad'an' is redundant in the definition of proper noun. But without it, the phrase 'if its meaning is one' would be obscure because it would only apply to words with a single simple meaning without necessary concomitants, which are rare. Furthermore, a word could then be described as univocal or amphibolous with respect to non-assigned meanings, which is external. Finally, al-Sharnubi raises a problem: pronouns, demonstratives, and relatives are universal in wad' according to the author, so how can their meanings be individuated externally while they are universal? The resolution is that these words are excluded by the condition 'then with its individuation' because they are used for particulars only in usage, not in wad'. But if one holds (like al-Sayyid and al-'Adud) that these are particulars in wad' and usage, then they are excluded by the first condition 'if its meaning is one', not by 'wad'an'. The commentary thus parses the precise role of each condition in the definition.

وضع
كلي
جزئي

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why is the restriction 'wad'an' necessary in the definition of a proper noun?
A) To exclude words that have multiple meanings.
B) To exclude words that are universal in linguistic convention but become particular only through usage, like pronouns.
C) To include words that are mentally individuated.
D) To ensure the meaning is not metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
The restriction 'wad'an' ensures that only words whose particularity is inherent in their original linguistic convention count as proper nouns, excluding those that become particular only through usage.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Excluding Pronouns, Demonstratives, and Relative Pronouns
Commentators explain why pronouns, demonstratives, and relative pronouns are not proper nouns.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why pronouns, demonstratives, and relative pronouns are not proper nouns under the author's view, and how the wad'an restriction achieves this exclusion.

Core Idea
Pronouns are universal in linguistic convention and become particular only in usage, so they are excluded by the wad'an condition.

The commentary focuses on the three categories of words that appear to be proper nouns because they refer to specific individuals: pronouns (like huwa), demonstratives (like hadha), and relative pronouns (like alladhi). According to the author of the matn, these words are universal in their original linguistic assignment (wad') and only gain particular reference through usage. Therefore, the wad'an restriction removes them from the definition of 'alam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The passage names: الضمير (pronoun), اسم الإشارة (demonstrative), and اسم الموصول (relative pronoun). Recognize them as words that can refer to specific individuals in context.
2
Understand the author's position on wad'
Al-Dasuqi states that according to the author (المصنف), these words are 'كليات وضعاً' (universals in wad') and 'جزئيات استعمالاً' (particulars in usage). They have a general meaning set by linguistic convention, but their specific referent is determined by the context of use.
For example, 'alladhi' is placed for the singular masculine in general; its specific referent comes from the relative clause.
3
See how they are excluded by wad'an
Since the individuation (tashakhkhus) required for a proper noun must be by wad' (original convention), these words fail because their individuation is accidental (عارض) due to usage. Therefore, they are excluded by the condition 'wad'an'.
Without the wad'an condition, they would satisfy the tashakhkhus condition because they refer to specific individuals in speech.
4
Contrast with the view of al-Sayyid and al-'Adud
The passage notes that according to al-Sayyid and al-'Adud, these words are 'جزئيات وضعاً واستعمالاً' (particulars in wad' and usage). In their view, the words are excluded by the first condition 'if its meaning is one', not by 'wad'an'. This shows how the understanding of wad' affects classification.
This contrast underscores the importance of the linguistic theory adopted.

Commentary

Why Pronouns are Not Proper Nouns
Commentary explains 'لا عارضاً' and exclusion of pronouns and demonstratives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why pronouns and demonstratives are not proper nouns according to the author's position, and identify the role of usage versus coinage.

Core Idea
Proper nouns are particular by coinage; pronouns are not proper nouns because their particularity is from usage.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies a key phrase 'not accidental' in the definition of proper nouns. He explains that pronouns and demonstratives are excluded because their particularity is not inherent in their coinage but arises from usage. We will explore the logical rationale and the ensuing scholarly debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Find the definiendum: the proper noun (العلم). The definition is: a word that signifies a particular individual by coinage without being accidental.
2
Understand the condition 'not accidental' (لا عارضاً)
This condition means that the particularity must come from the coinage itself, not from external factors like usage. The commentator immediately gives examples: pronouns and demonstratives.
3
Recognize the examples: pronouns and demonstratives
Pronouns (e.g., ana, anta) and demonstratives (e.g., hadha) refer to specific individuals, but their meanings as words are general concepts. Their particularity comes from the context of speech, not from the word itself.
4
Grasp the author's position on these words
According to the author, pronouns and demonstratives are universals by coinage (their original meaning is a concept) but become particulars by usage. Thus, they fail the condition 'not accidental'.
5
See the exclusion: they are not proper nouns
Because their particularity is accidental (from usage), they are excluded from the category of proper nouns. The rest of the passage discusses a philosophical objection to this view.

(قَوْلُهُ : لَا عَارِضَاً ) أي : بواسطة الاستعمال كَمَا في المضمراتِ وأسماء الإشارة ونظائرهما؛ بناءً على مختارِ المصنّف فيها مِنْ أنَّها كُلِّيَّاتٌ وَضْعاً؛ جُزئيات استعمالاً، وقد سبق أنَّ التَّقسيمَ هُنا جارٍ على ذلك الاصطلاح، فيكون التقييد بذلك لإخراجِهَا عَنِ العِلْم ، فإِنَّ التَّشخُصَ في مدلولاتها ليسَ مِنَ الوضع، بَل مِنَ الاستعمالِ، وَهَهُنا بحث أورده مير زاهد على المذهب الذي حققه المتأخرون فيها، وهو أَنَّهُ مُخَالِفٌ لِمَا ذهب إليهِ الشَّيْخُ وكثيرٌ مِنَ المحققينَ مِنْ أَنَّ الألفاظ موضوعةٌ لِلصُّوَرِ الدّهنيَّةِ دونَ الأعيان الخارجيَّةِ؛ لأنَّ الصُّورة الحاصِلَةَ في الذِّهْنِ هِيَ المعنى الكُلِّيُّ الصَّادقُ على الجزئيات الغير المتناهية، قال: وكانَ مُرَادُهُم بِالصُّوَرِ الذَّهنيَّةِ هَهُنَا نَفْسَ الشَّيْء مِنْ حيث هو؛ سواء كانَ حاصلاً في الذِّهْنِ بِنَفْسِهِ أو بوجه ما . فإِنْ قُلْتَ : هذا التَّحقيقُ يدلُّ على أن لا تكونُ الألفاظ موضوعةٌ لِمَا هو مَعلومٌ حقيقةً؛ فإِنَّ الجزئيَّاتِ معلومةٌ بِوَجهِ كُلّيّ، فيكونُ ذَلِكَ الوجه في الحقيقة معلوماً دونَ الجزئياتِ؛ ضَرورة أنَّ ما يحصلُ في الذَّهنِ مِنْ عِلْم الشَّيء بالوجه هو لوجه دونَ الشَّيء؛ قُلْتُ : الموضوعُ له يجب أن يكون مقصوداً بالذَّاتِ؛ سواء كان معلوماً بالذَّاتِ أو بالعَرَضِ، كَمَا أنَّ المحكوم عليهِ كَذلِكَ؛ فَتَأَمَّلْ. (١) (قولُ العطَّارِ : فيكونُ ... إلخ) فيه أنَّ الموضوع لهُ كُلّي عند المصنِّفِ، وهو يُنافي التّشخُصَ قطعاً، فهي خارجةٌ بِهِ لا بـ: وضعاً، كما لا يَخفَى ا.هـ. الشَّرنوبي.
(His statement: 'not accidental') meaning: by way of usage, as in pronouns, demonstratives, and their likes; based on the author's chosen position regarding them, that they are universals by coinage, particulars by usage. It has preceded that the division here proceeds according to that convention. So the restriction is to exclude them from being proper nouns, because the individuation in their referents is not from coinage but from usage. And here there is a research presented by Mir Zahid against the doctrine that the later scholars verified regarding them, which is that it contradicts what the Shaykh and many of the verifiers held, that words are coined for mental forms, not for external individuals; because the form obtained in the mind is the universal meaning that applies to infinite particulars. He said: 'Their intention by mental forms here is the thing itself insofar as it is, whether it exists in the mind itself or in some manner.' If you say: 'This verification indicates that words are not coined for what is known in reality; because particulars are known through a universal aspect, so that aspect is in reality known, not the particulars; necessarily, what is obtained in the mind of knowledge of the thing through an aspect is the aspect, not the thing.' I say: 'The coined-for must be intended per se, whether it is known per se or accidentally, just as the subject of judgment is likewise.' So reflect. (Footnote: (1) (Attar's statement: 'so it is ... etc.') In it, the coined-for is universal according to the author, and this definitely contradicts individuation, so they are excluded by it, not by 'waḍ‘an', as is not hidden. End. —Al-Sharnubi.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the phrase 'not accidental' in the definition of a proper noun. It specifies that 'not accidental' means that the particularity is not acquired through usage, as in the case of pronouns (e.g., 'I', 'you') and demonstratives (e.g., 'this', 'that'). According to the author, these words are universal in coinage (i.e., their original meaning is a concept) but become particular through usage (when used to refer to specific individuals). Therefore, they are excluded from being proper nouns because their particularity is not from coinage. The commentary then presents a research by Mir Zahid that challenges the later scholars' view that such words are universal in coinage. Mir Zahid argues that this contradicts the position of the Shaykh (possibly Ibn Sina or another authority) and many verificiers, who held that words are coined for mental forms, which are universals that apply to infinite particulars. The mental form is the thing itself considered in itself. A hypothetical objection is raised: if words are coined for mental forms, then they are not coined for actual particulars, because particulars are only known through a universal aspect. The response is that the object of coinage must be intended per se, regardless of whether it is known directly or indirectly. The footnote by Al-Sharnubi clarifies that according to the author, the coined-for is universal, which contradicts individuation, so pronouns and demonstratives are excluded from being proper nouns by being universal, not by the condition 'not accidental'. This shows a nuance in the logical theory.

المضمرات
أسماء الإشارة

Key Takeaway
Pronouns and demonstratives are excluded from being proper nouns because their particularity is accidental (from usage), not from coinage.

The Logical Definition of a Proper Noun: Personal vs Generic
Commentary defines 'علم' as particular proper noun and distinguishes it from generic proper noun.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a personal proper noun and a generic proper noun in the context of Islamic logic, and explain why logicians prefer the term 'particular' over 'proper noun'.

Core Idea
In logic, only personal proper nouns are true proper nouns; generic proper nouns are universals.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies that the term 'علم' in logic refers specifically to personal proper nouns like Zayd and Amr, which designate unique individuals. He also addresses the generic proper noun (علم الجنس), explaining why it is not considered a proper noun in logic but is included by grammarians. This distinction between the two fields is crucial for understanding how terms function in logical analysis versus grammatical analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
The passage defines 'علم' (proper noun) in the context of logic. Note that it immediately specifies it as 'شخصي' (personal), giving examples like Zayd and Amr. This tells you that the logical definition is narrow.
2
Distinguish personal from generic proper nouns
A personal proper noun (علم شخصي) designates a single individual (e.g., Zayd). A generic proper noun (علم جنسي) designates a class or species (e.g., 'Usāma' for lion) but is treated as a proper noun by grammarians. In logic, a generic proper noun is actually a univocal universal (كلي متواطئ) because it applies to every member of that class.
Example: 'أسامة' is a generic proper noun for lion, but in logic it is a universal term, not a particular.
3
Understand the different perspectives of logicians and grammarians
Logicians focus on meaning (المعنى بالقصد الأول), so they see that the meaning of a generic proper noun is universal, hence it is not a proper noun. Grammarians focus on verbal rulings (الأحكام اللفظية), such as definiteness, so they treat generic proper nouns as proper nouns. This is a case of convergence of terminologies (تحالف الاصطلاحين) due to different perspectives.
Similar to how the word 'وجود' (existence) has different meanings in different sciences.
4
Examine the two views on generic proper nouns
The passage presents two positions: (1) If generic proper nouns are considered to be applied truthfully to individuals (like 'human' applied to all humans), then their meaning is universal and they are not proper nouns. (2) If they are considered coined for the reality with the condition of mental unity (بشرط الوحدة الذهنية), then they are individuated and become genuine particulars, thus fitting the logical definition of proper noun.
The second view resolves the conflict but is less common.
5
Evaluate the definition's completeness
The definition of 'علم' as a personal proper noun includes all instances like Zayd and Amr. It excludes generic proper nouns under the logical perspective. However, the text allows that generic proper nouns may be included under 'and their likes' if one adopts the second view. Thus the definition is context-dependent.
The logician's preferred term is 'جزئي' (particular) instead of 'علم' to avoid confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(فَعَلَمْ) كزيدٍ، وعَمْرو، وأمثالهما الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : عَلَمٌ ) أي : شخصي؛ لتشخُص مدلولِهِ، وأمَّا عَلَمُ الجنس؛ فهو من الكُلِّيّ المتواطِئ، والأَوْلَى أنْ يعبّر بجزئي بدلَ عَلَم؛ لأنَّه هو وظيفة المنطقي، وأمَّا التَّعبيرُ بِعَلَم؛ فهو وظيفةُ النَّحوي . العطار (قَوْلُهُ : فَعَلَمٌ) أي : شخصي، وأمَّا العلمُ الجنسي فَليسَ علماً في عُرْفِ المنطقِ؛ لأنَّ نظرهم إلى المعنى بالقصْدِ الأوَّلِ ومعناه كُلّي، وإنَّما أدخلَهُ أهلُ العربيَّةِ في العلم نظراً إلى الأحكام اللفظيَّةِ، وهذا من باب تَحالُفِ الإصلاحَيْنِ بسببِ اختلافِ النَّظرَيْن كما في الكلماتِ الوُجوديَّةِ، هذا إذا مُجوِّزَ إطلاق العلم الجنسي حقيقةً على الأفرادِ كَمَا هو التَّحقيقُ، كَإطلاقِ الإنسانِ على أفرادِهِ، فَإِنَّ الإطلاق يكونُ باعتبارِ وَضْعِهِ لِلمعنى الكُلِّي الصَّادِقِ عليها، فيكون معناه كُلِّيَّا، أمَّا إذا لم يُجَوِّز ذلكَ وقِيلَ : إِنَّها موضوعةٌ لِلحقيقة بشرط الوحدة الذهنية؛ فهو بِهذا الاعتبارِ مُشخّص؛ ضَرورةً كَونِهِ جزئيا حقيقيًّا مُتَشخُصاً بالتَّشخُص الذهني، وحينئذٍ لا إشكال في تعريف العلم لصدقِهِ على جميع الأعلام الجنسية ودخولها فيه . (قَوْلُهُ : كَزَيْدٍ وَعَمْرِو) قضيَّةُ الاقتصار على التَّمثيل بِهِمَا أنَّ المراد العلمُ الشَّخصي، وقد علمت حال العلم الجنسي، ويحتمل دخوله تحتَ قَوْلِهِ : (وأمثالهما).
(So a proper noun) like Zayd and Amr and their likes. Al-Dussuqi: (His statement: a proper noun) i.e., personal, due to the individuation of its referent. As for the generic proper noun, it is from the univocal universal. It is better to express it with 'particular' instead of 'proper noun', because that is the function of the logician. As for the expression 'proper noun', it is the function of the grammarian. Al-‘Attār: (His statement: so a proper noun) i.e., personal; as for the generic proper noun, it is not a proper noun in the convention of logic, because their consideration is of the meaning with primary intention and its meaning is universal. Rather, the Arabic grammarians included it in proper nouns with a view to verbal rulings. And this is from the category of convergence of two terminologies due to difference of perspectives, as in existential words. This is if one permits the application of the generic proper noun as truth to individuals, as is the verification, like the application of 'human' to its individuals; for the application is by virtue of its coinage for the universal meaning that is true of them, so its meaning is universal. As for if one does not permit that and says: 'They are coined for the reality with the condition of mental unity,' then in this respect it is an individuator, necessarily being a genuine particular individuated by mental individuation. And in that case there is no difficulty in defining the proper noun, because it is true of all generic proper nouns and they are included in it. (His statement: 'like Zayd and Amr') The purport of limiting the examples to them is that what is intended is the personal proper noun. And you have known the status of the generic proper noun, and it is possible that it is included under his statement: 'and their likes.'
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'علم' (proper noun) as used in logic. The commentary begins by stating that 'علم' in the text refers to a personal proper noun, like Zayd and Amr, because its referent is individuated. It then distinguishes the 'generic proper noun' (e.g., 'Usāma' as a name for lion, which can apply to any lion) from the personal proper noun. Al-Dussuqi notes that the generic proper noun is actually a univocal universal (like 'human') and it is more appropriate for the logician to call it 'particular' rather than 'proper noun', because the term 'proper noun' is primarily a grammatical category. Al-‘Attār elaborates that in the convention of logic, a generic proper noun is not considered a proper noun because logicians consider meaning with primary intention, and the meaning of a generic proper noun is universal. Grammarians count it as a proper noun because they focus on verbal rulings. This difference is due to different perspectives, similar to terms like 'existence' which have different meanings in different fields. The passage then considers two views: if the generic proper noun is considered to be applied truthfully to individuals (like 'human' applied to all humans), then its meaning is universal. If instead it is considered to be coined for the reality with the condition of mental unity, then it becomes individuated and is a genuine particular, and then it would fit the definition of 'proper noun' without difficulty. The example of Zayd and Amr indicates that the intended meaning in the text is the personal proper noun, but the generic proper noun may also be included under 'and their likes'.

Key Takeaway
The logician defines a proper noun strictly as a term for a specific individual, while the grammarian includes generic proper nouns due to a different focus on verbal rulings.

Definition of 'Alam Shakhsi in Logic
Al-Dasuqi and al-'Attar define 'alam shakhsi and discuss 'alam jinsi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'alam shakhsi and 'alam jinsi, and explain why logicians prefer the term juz'i.

Core Idea
In logic, a proper noun is personal; generic proper nouns belong to grammar.

This passage from al-Dasuqi and al-'Attar clarifies the definition of 'alam (proper noun) in logic. While grammarians use 'alam for both personal and generic terms, logicians restrict it to terms indicating a specific individual. The commentators explain why the term juz'i (particular) is preferred and how generic proper nouns can be accommodated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Locate the term being defined: 'alam. Note that al-Dasuqi immediately specifies it as personal (shakhsi).
The passage begins: 'So a proper noun'.
2
Extract the differentia
What makes 'alam different from other terms? Its meaning is individuated (mutashakhkhas).
Al-Dasuqi says: 'because its meaning is individuated'.
3
Compare with grammar
Grammarians also use 'alam for generic terms (e.g., 'human'). In logic, such terms are universal (kulli) and univocal.
Al-Dasuqi contrasts the logician's focus on meaning with the grammarian's focus on linguistic form.
4
Understand the terminological shift
Al-Dasuqi advises using juz'i instead of 'alam to avoid confusion. Why? Because the logician prioritizes meaning, not form.
The shift alert in the key terms explains this.
5
Apply to examples
Zayd and 'Amr are personal proper nouns; 'insan' (human) would be generic. Determine which is 'alam in logic.
Only personal proper nouns qualify as 'alam shakhsi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعَلَمٌ كزيدٍ، وعَمْرو، وأمثالهما
الدسوقي: (قَوْلُهُ : عَلَمٌ ) أي : شخصي؛ لتشخُص مدلولِهِ، وأمَّا عَلَمُ الجنس؛ فهو من الكُلِّيّ المتواطِئ، والأَوْلَى أنْ يعبّر بجزئي بدلَ عَلم؛ لأنَّه هو وظيفة المنطقي، وأمَّا التَّعبيرُ بِعَلَم؛ فهو وظيفةُ النَّحوي.
العطار: لِلصُّوَرِ الدّهنيَّةِ دونَ الأعيان الخارجيَّةِ؛ لأنَّ الصُّورة الحاصِلَةَ في الذِّهْنِ هِيَ المعنى الكُلِّيُّ الصَّادقُ على الجزئيات الغير المتناهية، قال: وكانَ مُرَادُهُم بِالصُّوَرِ الذَّهنيَّةِ هَهُنَا نَفْسَ الشَّيْء مِنْ حيث هو؛ سواء كانَ حاصلاً في الذِّهْنِ بِنَفْسِهِ أو بوجه ما. فإِنْ قُلْتَ : هذا التَّحقيقُ يدلُّ على أن لا تكونُ الألفاظ موضوعةٌ لِمَا هو مَعلومٌ حقيقةً؛ فإِنَّ الجزئيَّاتِ معلومةٌ بِوَجهِ كُلّيّ، فيكونُ ذَلِكَ الوجه في الحقيقة معلوماً دونَ الجزئياتِ؛ ضَرورة أنَّ ما يحصلُ في الذَّهنِ مِنْ عِلْم الشَّيء بالوجه هو لوجه دونَ الشَّيء؛ قُلْتُ : الموضوعُ له يجب أن يكون مقصوداً بالذَّاتِ؛ سواء كان معلوماً بالذَّاتِ أو بالعَرَضِ، كَمَا أنَّ المحكوم عليهِ كَذلِكَ؛ فَتَأَمَّلْ.
(قَوْلُهُ : فَعَلَمٌ) أي : شخصي، وأمَّا العلمُ الجنسي فَليسَ علماً في عُرْفِ المنطقِ؛ لأنَّ نظرهم إلى المعنى بالقصْدِ الأوَّلِ ومعناه كُلّي، وإنَّما أدخلَهُ أهلُ العربيَّةِ في العلم نظراً إلى الأحكام اللفظيَّةِ، وهذا من باب تَحالُفِ الإصطلاحَيْنِ بسببِ اختلافِ النَّظرَيْن كما في الكلماتِ الوجوديَّةِ، هذا إذا مُجوِّزَ إطلاق العلم الجنسي حقيقةً على الأفرادِ كَمَا هو التَّحقيقُ، كَإطلاقِ الإنسانِ على أفرادِهِ، فَإِنَّ الإطلاق يكونُ باعتبارِ وَضْعِهِ لِلمعنى الكُلِّي الصَّادِقِ عليها، فيكون معناه كُلِّيَّا، أمَّا إذا لم يُجَوِّز ذلكَ وقِيلَ : إِنَّها موضوعةٌ لِلحقيقة بشرط الوحدة الذهنية؛ فهو بِهذا الاعتبارِ مُشخّص؛ ضَرورةً كَونِهِ جزئيا حقيقيًّا مُتَشخُصاً بالشَّخص الذهني، وحينئذٍ لا إشكال في تعريف العلم لصدقِهِ على جميع الأعلام الجنسية ودخولها فيه.
(قَوْلُهُ : كَزَيْدٍ وَعَمْرِو) قضيَّةُ الاقتصار على التَّمثيل بِهِمَا أنَّ المراد العلمُ الشَّخصي، وقد علمت حال العلم الجنسي، ويحتمل دخوله تحتَ قَوْلِهِ : (وأمثالهما).
'So a proper noun' like Zayd and 'Amr and their likes. Al-Dasuqi: (His saying: 'a proper noun') i.e., personal; because its meaning is individuated, and as for the generic proper noun, it is from the univocal universal, and it is better to express it as 'particular' instead of 'proper noun', because that is the business of the logician. As for the expression 'proper noun', it is the business of the grammarian. Al-'Attar: ...
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage defines the proper noun ('alam) as a term whose meaning is individuated. The commentators clarify that in logic, the proper noun is always personal ('alam shakhsi), not generic ('alam jinsi). Al-Dasuqi notes that logicians prefer the term 'particular' (juz'i) over 'proper noun' to avoid confusion with grammar. Al-'Attar expands on the relationship between mental forms and external entities, responding to a potential objection about whether words can signify objects that are known partially. The discussion emphasizes that the object of signification is intended intrinsically, even if known accidentally. The example of Zayd and 'Amr illustrates the personal proper noun, but it is noted that generic proper nouns (like 'human') may be included if considered with mental individuation.

C) Kulli
D) Mushtarak

Key Takeaway
In logic, 'alam is personal; generic proper nouns are considered universal and are not 'alam properly speaking.

Definition of Mutawati' (Univocal Term)
Definition of mutawati' (univocal term)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a mutawati' term and distinguish it from proper nouns and equivocal terms based on the condition of equality.

Core Idea
A univocal term applies equally to all its individuals, with no priority.

This passage defines mutawati' (univocal) as a term whose meaning holds equally across all its individuals, whether mental or external. This distinction is crucial for understanding how words relate to their meanings in logic and Islamic sciences. The commentators expand on the condition of equality and clarify its scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key condition
The passage states that a mutawati' term requires equality among its individuals in the occurrence and truth of the meaning. This means no individual is more entitled to the meaning than another.
The condition applies to both mental and external individuals.
2
Distinguish mental and external individuals
Mental individuals are hypothetical concepts that may not exist externally, while external individuals are actual existents. Equality must hold in both realms for the term to be univocal.
Al-'Attar notes that some terms like 'sun' may have only mental individuals, but the condition still applies.
3
Test with an example
Apply the condition to 'human': all humans are equally human, even if they differ in accidental attributes like knowledge or ignorance. This confirms 'human' as a mutawati' term.
This shows that equality in the core meaning does not preclude differences in accidents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[المتواطِئُ]
( وَبِدُونِهِ) عطفٌ على قولِهِ: «فمعَ تشخُصِه»؛ أي: المفرد إن اتَّحدّ معناه، فإن كانَ مع تشخص ذلك المعنى، فهو عَلَمٌ، وإن كانَ بدونِ تشخص، فهو إِمَّا مُتَوَاطِئُ إِنْ تَسَاوَتْ أَفْرَادُهُ) الذهنيَّةُ والخارجيَّةُ في حصوله وصدقه عليها،

(قَوْلُهُ : إِنْ تَسَاوَتْ أَفْرَادُهُ الذِّهْنِيَّةُ) أي: الفرضية التي لا وجود لها خارجاً، وقوله : (والخارجيَّة)؛ أي: الموجودة في الخارج، وقوله: (في حصوله)؛ أي: في حصولِ ذلك المعنى فيها؛ أي: في تلكَ الأفرادِ.

(قَوْلُهُ : فِي أَفْرَادِهِ الذَّهْنِيَّةِ) أي: الفرضيَّة، وإنْ كانَ يمتنع ذلك بسبب خارج عن مَفهومِ اللَّفْظِ كالشَّمسِ؛ كَذَا في «الشّفاء»، فالمراد بالخارجيَّةِ مَا يُقابِلُها؛ سواء كانت في الأعيان أو في الأذهان، فاتَّضَحَ أَنَّ لِلإنسان أفراداً خارجيَّةٌ لا ذهنية، ولِلشَّمس أفراد ذهنية، أفاده عبد الحكيم. A chapter: On investigations of words. [The Univocal] (And without it) is a conjunction attached to his saying: 'with its individuation'; i.e., the single term if its meaning is unified, then if it is with individuation of that meaning, it is a proper noun, and if it is without individuation, then it is either univocal if its individuals - mental and external - are equal in its occurrence and truth upon them. Al-Dasuqi: ... Al-'Attar: ...
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage defines the univocal term (mutawati') as a term whose meaning applies equally to all its individuals, without one being prioritized over another. The discussion distinguishes mental individuals (e.g., possible concepts) from external individuals (e.g., actual existents). Al-Dasuqi explains that the term 'univocal' is applied to the word metaphorically because its individuals are described as univocal. Al-'Attar clarifies that equality means no individual is more entitled to the meaning than another, though they may differ in accidental attributes (e.g., some humans are knowledgeable, some ignorant). The example of 'human' shows that all humans are equally human, even if some are scholars. The passage also notes that some terms like 'sun' may have only mental individuals due to external impossibility, but the condition of equality still applies.

Understanding the Univocal Term (Mutawāṭi')
Commentary defines the univocal term and its condition of equal application.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a univocal term and distinguish it from terms that apply with priority or superiority, using the condition of equal application to mental and external individuals.

Core Idea
A univocal term applies equally to all its instances without priority or superiority.

In Islamic logic, terms are classified by how they apply to individuals. The univocal term is a key category where the meaning applies equally to every instance. The commentator explains this using examples like 'human' and 'sun'. Understanding this distinction is essential for precise definitions in Islamic sciences like usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Find the condition of univocality
Look for the phrase 'if its individuals are equal in truth of the meaning upon them'. What does equality refer to?
2
Distinguish essential equality from accidental difference
Note that the commentator stresses equality in the concept itself, not in accidental attributes like knowledge and ignorance.
3
Apply to examples
Consider 'human': all humans are equally human, even if some are scholars and others ignorant. Confirm that the term applies equally to mental and external individuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ كَانَ بِدُوْنِ تَشَخْصٍ، فَهُوَ إِمَّا مُتَوَاطِئُ إِنْ تَسَاوَتْ أَفْرَادُهُ الذِّهْنِيَّةُ وَالْخَارِجِيَّةُ فِي حُصُولِهِ وَصِدْقِهِ عَلَيْهَا. (قَوْلُهُ: إِنْ تَسَاوَتْ أَفْرَادُهُ) أَيْ فِي صِدْقِ هَذَا الْمَعْنَى عَلَيْهَا؛ بِمَعْنَى أَنَّهُ لا يَكُونُ بَيْنَهَا تَفَاوُتٌ بِأَوَّلِيَّةٍ أَوْ أَوْلَوِيَّةٍ، وَإِنْ كَانَ بَيْنَهَا تَفَاوُتٌ بِوَجْهِ آخَرَ كَالْإِنْسَانِ؛ فَإِنَّ أَفْرَادَهُ الْمُنْدَرِجَةَ تَحْتَهُ لَيْسَتْ مُتَفَاوِتَةً بِأَحَدِ الْوَجْهَيْنِ الْآتِيَيْنِ فِي كَوْنِهَا إِنْسَاناً، وَإِنْ كَانَتْ مُتَفَاوِتَةً فِي الْعَوَارِضِ كَكَوْنِ بَعْضِهَا عَالِماً وَبَعْضِهَا جَاهِلاً. وَمِثَالُ المُتَوَاطِئِ كَالْإِنْسَانِ وَالشَّمْسِ، فَإِنَّ صِدْقَهُمَا عَلَى أَفْرَادِهِمَا الذِّهْنِيَّةِ وَالْخَارِجِيَّةِ بِالسَّوِيَّةِ، وَلَيْسَ بَعْضُ الْأَفْرَادِ أَوْلَى مِنْ بَعْضٍ.
And if it is without specification, then it is either univocal if its individuals—mental and external—are equal in the occurrence and truth of it upon them. (His statement: 'if its individuals are equal') meaning: in the truth of this meaning upon them; meaning that there is no difference between them in priority or superiority, even if there is difference in another aspect, like 'human'; for its individuals subsumed under it are not differentiated by either of the two upcoming aspects in being human, even if they differ in accidents, such as some being knowledgeable and some ignorant. And an example of the univocal is 'human' and 'sun', for their truth upon their mental and external individuals is equal, and no individual is more entitled than another.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage defines the univocal term (mutawāṭi') and explains its essential condition. It opens by stating that if a term is without specification (i.e., it is a universal), it is either univocal if its individuals—both mental (hypothetical) and external (actual)—are equal in the occurrence and truth of the meaning upon them. The commentator then clarifies the phrase 'if its individuals are equal' by emphasizing that equality here refers to the truth of the meaning upon them, meaning there is no difference in priority or superiority in the application of the concept. Even if individuals differ in accidental attributes like knowledge and ignorance, the core concept applies equally. The examples of 'human' and 'sun' illustrate that the meaning applies equally to all their individuals, whether mental or external; for instance, all humans are equally human, and the concept 'sun' applies equally to the real sun and to mental representations of it. The passage guards against the misunderstanding that equality in application requires equality in all attributes; rather, it only requires equality in the essential concept itself.

Key Terms
متواطئ (mutawāṭi'): A univocal term whose meaning applies equally to all its individuals without priority or superiority. [Note: In earlier logic texts, the term often contrasts with mushtarik (equivocal) and mushakkik (graded); this usage is standard.]
أفراد ذهنية (afrād dhihniyya): Mental individuals or hypothetical instances of a concept that exist only in the mind.
أفراد خارجية (afrād khārijiyya): External individuals that exist in reality outside the mind.
صدق (sidq): The application or truth of a concept to its individuals; here it means the concept holds true of them. [Note: In propositional logic, sidq often means truth of a statement; here it is used in the context of concepts applying to individuals.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It has both mental and external individuals.

Key Takeaway
A univocal term applies its meaning equally to all individuals, both mental and external, without priority or superiority, even if individuals differ in accidental attributes.

Univocal and Equivocal Terms: Definitions and the Reality Debate
The commentary defines univocal and equivocal terms and resolves an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish univocal (mutawati') from equivocal (mushakkik) terms and evaluate the objection that mushakkik has no reality.

Core Idea
The reality of mushakkik depends on whether disparity lies within the same kind as the quiddity.

This passage defines the two key types of universal terms—univocal and equivocal—and then addresses a deep objection: how can a term be equivocal if the disparity is either internal or external to the meaning? The answer distinguishes the 'kind' of disparity, clarifying the logical foundation of terms used in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining property of mutawati'
The passage states that a term is mutawati' when all individuals share the meaning equally. For example, 'human' applies to Zayd and Amr with the same humanity. Differences like knowledge or prophethood are accidental, not part of the core meaning.
This is the standard definition: equality in the core signification.
2
Extract the defining property of mushakkik
A term is mushakkik when individuals differ in priority or intensity of the meaning. For example, 'existence' is more true of the Necessary Being than contingent beings. The disparity is in the core meaning itself, not external.
The key is that the meaning is one but applied with gradation.
3
Analyze the objection against mushakkik
Ibn al-Tilimsani and others argue that mushakkik has no reality because either the disparity is part of the meaning (making it mushtarak/sharik) or it is external (making it mutawati'). They see no third option.
The objection forces a dilemma: either the word is truly shared or truly univocal.
4
Reconstruct the response to the objection
The response chooses the second horn (word is placed for common meaning, disparity is external) but denies that it makes the term mutawati'. Why? Because in mushakkik, the disparity is in something of the same kind (jins) as the concept, whereas in mutawati' disparity is in a different kind (accidental).
The criterion: if the cause of disparity is of the same kind as the quiddity → mushakkik; if external → mutawati'.
5
Apply the criterion to an Islamic example
Test with 'wujūd' (existence): the quiddity is existence itself. Disparity between God's existence and creatures' existence is of the same kind (existence) but with priority. Therefore, it is mushakkik. In contrast, 'insān' (human): humanity is equal; disparity in knowledge is accidental → mutawati'.
This concrete application solidifies the logical distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مباحثِ الألفاظ. وسُمِّي متواطئاً ؛ لتوافق الأفرادِ في معناه منَ التَّواطؤ، وهو التَّوافق . قال الدسوقي: (قَوْلُهُ : لِتَوَافُقِ الْأَفْرَادِ فِي مَعْنَاهُ أي : في معنى ذلك اللفظ المفرد، ومعناه: هو الأمرُ الكُلّي، فحظ زيدٍ مِنَ الإنسانيَّةِ كَحَظِّ عمرو منها، والقدر الحاصل منها في العالِمِ كَالحاصل منها في الجاهل، والحاصل منها في الأنبياء كالحاصل منها في غَيْرِهِم، وَالِاخْتِلَافُ إنَّما هو بعوارض خارجة عن الإنسانية؛ كَالعِلْمِ والجهلِ والنُّبُوَّةِ والصلاح وغير ذلك). (و) إِمَّا (مُشَكِّكٌ إِنْ تَفَاوَتَتِ) الأفراد في حصوله وصدقه عليها، بأن كان حصوله في بعض الأفراد أَوْلَى من بعض. قال ابنُ التَّلمساني: «لا حقيقةَ لِلمُشكك»، وكذا السَّيِّدُ في حواشي المطالع ، والعلامة اليوسي في الانتصار له. وحاصلُهُ : أَنَّ مَا بِهِ التَّفاوت ؛ إنْ كانَ داخلاً فيما وضع له اللفظ؛ فَمُشترك، وإلا يكن داخلاً فيما يوضع له اللفظ ، بل اللفظ إنَّما وضعَ لِلقدْرِ المشترك بين الأفراد؛ فَمتواطئ. وقد أُجيب عنه باختيار الشَّقِّ الثَّاني، وهو أنَّ اللَّفظَ مَوضوع للقدْرِ المشترك، وأَنَّ مَا بِهِ التَّفاوت ليس داخلاً فيما وضعَ له اللفظ، لكنَّهُ غَيرُ مُتواطِئ؛ لأَنَّ مَا تفاوتتْ فيه الأفرادُ مِن جنسِ مَفهوم اللفظ الموضوع له والمتواطئ؛ إنَّما تتفاوتُ أفراده في أمورٍ ليست من جنس المفهوم. والحاصلُ : أَنَّ مَا بِهِ التَّفاوتُ إنْ كانَ مِنْ جنس الماهيَّة؛ كانَ مُشكّكَاً، وإِنْ كانَ خارجاً عنها ؛ كانَ مُتواطِئَاً.
A chapter: On investigations of words. And it is called 'mutawati' (univocal) due to the agreement of individuals in its meaning from 'tawatu', which is agreement. Al-Dasuqi said: (His statement: 'for the agreement of individuals in its meaning' means in the meaning of that singular word, and its meaning is the universal thing. So the share of Zayd from humanity is like the share of Amr from it, and the amount present in the scholar is like the amount present in the ignorant, and the amount present in the prophets is like the amount present in others. The difference is only due to accidents external to humanity, such as knowledge, ignorance, prophethood, righteousness, and others). (And) it is either (mushakkik (equivocal) if the individuals differ) in its occurrence and truthfulness upon them, such that its occurrence in some individuals is more primary than in others. Ibn al-Tilimsani said: 'There is no reality for the equivocal,' and likewise al-Sayyid in his glosses on al-Mutali', and al-Allama al-Yusi in his defense of it. Its summary: that the cause of disparity: if it is included in what the word is placed for, then it is shared (mushtarak); otherwise, it is not included in what the word is placed for, but the word is only placed for the common amount among the individuals, then it is univocal. And it was answered by choosing the second alternative, that the word is placed for the common amount, and that the cause of disparity is not included in what the word is placed for, but it is not univocal; because that in which the individuals differ is of the same kind as the concept of the word placed for it, whereas the univocal has its individuals differing in matters that are not of the same kind as the concept. The conclusion: that the cause of disparity, if it is of the same kind as the quiddity, is equivocal; and if it is external to it, then it is univocal.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage defines two types of universal terms: univocal (mutawati') and equivocal (mushakkik). It also presents a critical objection and answer. The passage begins by stating that a term is called mutawati' (univocal) due to the agreement of its individuals in its meaning, such as 'human' applied to Zayd and Amr equally. Al-Dasuqi explains that this equality is in the core meaning (humanity), while differences in knowledge, prophethood, etc., are accidental and external. Then the passage defines mushakkik (equivocal) as a term whose individuals differ in the degree of its meaning, like 'existence' being more true of the Necessary Being than of contingent beings. Ibn al-Tilimsani and others object that there is no reality to the equivocal; they argue that if the cause of disparity is part of the meaning, it is shared (mushtarak), and if not, it is univocal. The response chooses the second horn: the word is placed for the common meaning, but it is not univocal because in the equivocal the disparity is in the same kind as the concept (e.g., existence is the same concept but applied with priority), while in the univocal the disparity is in external accidents. Thus, the conclusion distinguishes: if the cause of disparity is of the same nature (jins) as the quiddity, it is equivocal; if external, it is univocal.

Key Terms
متواطئ
مشكك
تواطؤ
تشكيك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a term considered mushakkik?
A) When its individuals share the meaning equally.
B) When the cause of disparity is of the same kind as the quiddity.
C) When the word has multiple unrelated meanings.
D) When the disparity is due to external accidents.

Key Takeaway
Univocal terms share meaning equally; equivocal terms share meaning with priority/posteriority, resolved by whether the disparity is of the same kind as the essence.

?
Identify whether the term 'qādir' (powerful) applied to God and humans is mutawati' or mushakkik, and explain your reasoning using the criterion from the passage.

Understanding Mushakkik and Refuting Its Denial
Defines mushakkik and answers the objection that it has no reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish mushakkik from mutawāṭiʾ and refute the objection that mushakkik has no reality.

Core Idea
Mushakkik is real: the differentia is of the same genus as the essence.

In this lesson, we explore the concept of mushakkik (equivocal term) as opposed to mutawāṭiʾ (univocal term). The passage defines mushakkik as a term whose individuals differ in the degree of applicability, with the difference being of the same genus as the meaning. It then presents and refutes an objection by Ibn al-Tilimsānī that mushakkik has no reality. Understanding this distinction is crucial for precise logical analysis in Islamic sciences, especially in kalām and uṣūl al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of mushakkik
Read the definition: a term is mushakkik if its individuals differ in the occurrence and truth of the meaning upon them, i.e., the meaning applies to some more primarily than to others. Note that the difference (tafāwut) is not accidental but of the same genus as the essence.
2
Identify the objection against mushakkik
Ibn al-Tilimsānī argued that mushakkik has no reality: if the differentiating factor is included in the meaning, the term is ambiguous (mushtarak); if not, it is univocal (mutawāṭiʾ). So no third category exists.
3
Analyze the response
The response accepts the second horn (the word is for the common meaning, differentia not included) but denies that this makes it mutawāṭiʾ. The key point: in mushakkik, the differentia is of the same genus as the concept, whereas in mutawāṭiʾ, differences are external to the essence.
The differentia being 'min jins al-māhiyya' (of the genus of the essence) is the distinguishing feature.
4
Apply to an Islamic example
Consider 'wujūd' (existence): it applies to God more primarily than to creatures, and the difference in intensity is of the same genus as existence itself. Hence, 'wujūd' is mushakkik, not mutawāṭiʾ.

Source Text

المشكك (و) إِمَّا (مُشَكِّكٌ إِنْ تَفَاوَتَتِ) الأفراد في حصوله وصدقه عليها، بأن كان حصوله في بعض الأفراد أولى من بعض. الدسوقي غيرهم، والاختلافُ إنَّما هو بعوارض خارجة عن الإنسانية؛ كَالعِلْمِ والجهلِ والنُّبُوَّةِ والصلاح وغير ذلك . (قَوْلُهُ : وَأَمَّا مُشَكِّكٌ قالَ ابنُ التَّلمساني: «لا حقيقةَ لِلمُشكك»، وكذا السَّيِّدُ في حواشي المطالع ، والعلامة اليوسي في الانتصار له . وحاصلُهُ : أَنَّ مَا بِهِ التَّفاوت ؛ إنْ كانَ داخلاً فيما وضع له اللفظ؛ فَمُشترك، وإلا ؛ يكن داخلاً فيما يوضع له اللفظ ، بل اللفظ إنَّما وضعَ لِلقدْرِ المشترك بين الأفراد؛ فَمتواطئ. وقد أُجيب عنه باختيار الشَّقِّ الثَّاني، وهو أنَّ اللَّفظَ مَوضوع للقدْرِ المشترك، وأَنَّ مَا بِهِ التَّفاوت ليس داخلاً فيما وضعَ له اللفظ، لكنَّهُ غَيرُ مُتواطِئ؛ لأَنَّ مَا تفاوتتْ فيه الأفرادُ مِن جنسِ مَفهوم اللفظ الموضوع له والمتواطئ؛ إنَّما تتفاوتُ أفراده في أمورٍ ليست من جنس المفهوم. والحاصلُ : أَنَّ مَا بِهِ التَّفاوتُ إنْ كانَ مِنْ جنس الماهيَّة؛ كانَ مُشكّكَاً، وإِنْ كانَ خارجاً عنها ؛ كانَ مُتواطِئَاً . (قَوْلُهُ : وَإِمَّا مُشَكِّكٌ) أي : وإما أن يكون ذلك المفرد الَّذي اتَّحد معناه وكانَ غيرَ مُشخّص في الخارج مُشكّكاً، وقوله: (إن تفاوت الأفراد)؛ أي: أفراد ذلكَ المعنى الغير المشخّص ، وقولُهُ: (في حصوله)؛ أي: ذلك المعنى في تلك الأفراد، وقولُه : وصدقُهُ ( عليها ) ؛ أي: وتحققه فيها، وهذا تفسيرُ لما قبله، فالمراد بحصولِ ذلك المعنى في الأفراد ؛ تحققه فيها . وقولُهُ : (بأن كانَ الباء فيه للتَّصوير ؛ أي: تفاوت الأفراد في حصول المعنى فيها مُصوَّرٌ بكون حصولِ المعنى في بعض الأفرادِ أَوْلَى مِن حصولِهِ في بعض آخر .
The equivocal (mushakkik): (And) either (equivocal if the individuals differ) in its occurrence and truth upon them, i.e., that its occurrence in some individuals is more prior (awla) than in others. Al-Dasuqi: Others, and the difference is only through accidents external to humanity, such as knowledge, ignorance, prophethood, righteousness, etc. (His saying: And as for mushakkik) Ibn al-Tilimsani said: 'There is no reality for the mushakkik,' and likewise al-Sayyid in his glosses on al-Matali', and al-Allama al-Yusi in his support of him. The summary: that that by which the difference occurs; if it is included in what the word is placed for, then it is shared (mushtarak), otherwise it is not included in what the word is placed for, but rather the word is placed for the common amount among the individuals, so it is univocal (mutawati'). And it was answered by choosing the second alternative, which is that the word is placed for the common amount, and that that by which the difference occurs is not included in what the word is placed for, but it is not univocal; because that in which the individuals differ is of the genus of the concept the word is placed for, while the univocal's individuals only differ in matters not of the genus of the concept. The conclusion: that that by which the difference occurs, if it is of the genus of the essence, then it is equivocal; if it is external to it, then it is univocal. (His saying: And as for mushakkik) meaning: and that the simple term whose meaning is unified and is not individuated in external existence be equivocal. And his saying: (if the individuals differ) meaning: the individuals of that non-individuated meaning. And his saying: (in its occurrence) meaning: that meaning in those individuals. And his saying: and its truth (upon them) meaning: its realization in them. This is an interpretation of what preceded, so what is meant by the occurrence of that meaning in the individuals is its realization in them. And his saying: (i.e., the ba is for illustration) meaning: the difference of the individuals in the occurrence of the meaning in them is illustrated by the occurrence of the meaning in some individuals being more prior than its occurrence in others.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'mushakkik' (equivocal) as opposed to 'mutawati' (univocal). It begins with the matn: a term is mushakkik if its individuals differ in the degree to which the meaning applies to them, i.e., it applies to some more primarily than to others. The commentary by al-Dasuqi clarifies that differences like knowledge or ignorance are accidental, not essential. Then an objection from Ibn al-Tilimsani is presented: that mushakkik has no reality. The objection argues that if the differentiating factor is included in the meaning, the term is ambiguous (mushtarak), and if not, it is univocal; thus no third category exists. The answer chooses the second horn: the word is for the common meaning, but it is not univocal because the differentia is of the same genus as the concept, unlike truly univocal terms whose differences are external. The conclusion: if the differentia is of the same genus as the essence, it is mushakkik; if external, it is mutawati'. The commentary then parses each phrase, emphasizing that the difference is illustrated by the meaning being more prior in some individuals. An Islamic example: 'wujud' (existence) applies to God more primarily than to creatures, hence mushakkik, while 'insan' (human) applies equally to all humans, hence mutawati'.

مُتَوَاطِئ
تَفَاوُت
مَاهِيَّة

B) The differentia in mushakkik is of the same genus as the essence.

D) Mutawāṭiʾ has individuals differing in priority.

Key Takeaway
Mushakkik is a genuine category: the differentia is of the same genus as the essence, distinguishing it from both mutawāṭiʾ and mushtarak.
